## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting mechanical stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a classic problem in materials science and solid mechanics. The relationship captures how material deformation behavior depends on both the amount of strain and the thermal conditions, encompassing phenomena like thermal softening, elastic-plastic transitions, and temperature-dependent moduli.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood or Hollomon strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook static term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T + c4 * T**2) (strain hardening with thermal softening polynomial)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature softening)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (exponential saturation hardening)
- Voce with thermal dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening with T-dependent yield)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Thermally activated flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation combined with hardening)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or hyperelastic expansion)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (exponential thermal softening with linear elasticity)
- Coupled power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature effects)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (Garofalo/hyperbolic sine creep law form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress with increasing temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → sigma ~ epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 indicating work hardening in metals
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) representing initial yield before hardening onset
- Temperature-strain separability → Product form sigma = g(epsilon) * h(T) when thermal and mechanical effects are decoupled
- Pre-strain or initial strain offset → (epsilon + c)**n form capturing prior deformation history
- High-temperature creep regime → Hyperbolic sine or exponential dependence on temperature indicating thermally activated dislocation motion
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Piecewise or smooth transition using tanh(c*epsilon) to blend linear and nonlinear regimes
